電影小說四十一街４２ＮＤＳＴＲＥＥＴ（四）

— 思蘋

歌舞練習散班的時候，潘特還在戲院外面。潘特眼見着陶樂賽偕着亞布納狄龍跑開，心　覺得懊喪，但是他看見了潘琪的時候，精神又大爲振作。潘特比皮萊年紀大些，但在某一點上也比他漂亮些。潘特向潘琪略加勾引，便同她去吃夜飯。晚餐後，他們又同乘公共汽車回到四十二街，彼此談來已成知己。潘琪見着潘特有點悶悶不樂，就問他什麽事使他傷心。潘特便慘笑着把他同另外一個成功的歌舞女星的戀愛史傾心相告，並且請求她對這事的意見，潘琪便勸他重新做起。

在關閉房門以前，潘琪頻頻回顧，表示默視潘特晚安。在她再後一顧的當兒，她幣見街沿石上兩個黑影迫近他的身子。其中一個恰發出聲音說話。

「我們有一個信帶給呌潘特但寗的，」他恐嚇着說。「倘使他不丢開陶樂賽布樂克，那就要給他一個難看丨丨但寗，知道沒有？」

對方面回答一言未了，那個人便右手伸，重重地給潘特一拳。潘特應聲跌倒在地，第一個流氓立卽跳人等待着的汽車，第二個流氓却仍停留着用力痛踢跌倒的人的肚旁骨，然後跟着躍人汽車揚長而去。

潘琪驚駭而呌，奔下階沿扶起潘特。

第二天潘特便接受費城戲院的聘請，準備同陶樂賽不别而行。但在潘特　擋行裝的時候，陶樂賽却突然蒞止。

潘特覺得心裏重甸甸的沒有勇氣同她吻别，因爲他知道，她也知道，一吻之後，他們彼此就會括不了的呀。潘特起身走到　邊。陶樂賽也沒有揩乾她的眼涙，便盲目的向門摸去。　　「再會，潘特，」他鳴烟着說。

潘特並沒回頭。（未完）

1933.05.03

Commemorating the May Third Incident

Today marks the fifth anniversary of the May Third Jinan Massacre. The occurrence of the May Third Incident was due to the expansion of revolutionary forces in our country. As the Northern Warlords were successively overthrown, the power of imperialists in China also began to waver. Therefore, when the National Revolutionary Army's second Northern Expedition progressed to Shandong, Japanese imperialists brazenly revealed their true aggressive colors under the guise of "protecting overseas Chinese." They openly dispatched troops to Shandong for the second time to secretly aid the warlords and obstruct the progress of revolutionary forces. At the same time, they occupied Jinan, indiscriminately bombing, slaughtering, and wreaking havoc. In this page of tragic and humiliating history, we can clearly see that imperialists, in order to maintain their interests in colonies, will exert all their strength to suppress the revolutionary forces in those colonies and support their existing powers. The occurrence of the May Third Incident was precisely the implementation of this aggressive policy.

"May Third" marks its fifth anniversary today, meaning we have commemorated "May Third" four times in the past. What have we gained from those four commemorations? Blood and tears, sighs, meaningless moans, and futile anger. However, the humiliation of the old "May Third" has not been washed away in the slightest, and new national humiliations continue to unfold. Since September 18th, the humiliation our nation has suffered is ten or a hundred times greater than that of "May Third." The oppression and trampling of our country by Japanese imperialists is also ten or a hundred times greater than that of "May Third." Old wounds have not healed, and new wounds cover our entire body. Therefore, will our commemoration of "May Third" today be just like the past four times, a mere formality? Will we continue to weep and lament, simply offering another memorial to the past?

We believe that commemorating "May Third" today is of even greater significance than in the past. Firstly, due to the intensification of the capitalist economic crisis, imperialists, in order to struggle for their dying breaths, are not only suppressing revolutionary forces and supporting existing powers in colonies and semi-colonies, but are also demanding a re-division of colonies. Thus, our country, the center of the Far East problem, is surrounded by the world and finds itself in an extremely difficult and precarious situation. Secondly, since September 18th, Japanese imperialists have intensified their aggression against us step by step, but our entire country has not been able to actively resist them. The enemy's desires are endless, while our dreams of complacency continue. This is no different than showing that our nation has lost its ability to maintain its survival and is willing to be slaughtered. Therefore, the practical problem facing us today is how to resist the aggression of Japanese imperialists and how to strive for the survival and freedom of our nation.

In summary, under the current circumstances, the only way for us to wash away the humiliations of the past is through resistance. The only way to maintain the survival of our nation is also through "resistance." Only resistance is enough to commemorate the past "May Third," and only resistance is enough to stop the continued unfolding of new national humiliations. Otherwise, what is the point of commemoration? What is the point of moaning?

Roosevelt's Focus

Shifts to the Far East Question

Yenching University President Summoned to the White House

To Contribute Opinions on the Sino-Japanese Dispute

Minister Song to Arrive in the US Within Days

Gu and Guo's Trip to Washington Cancelled

WASHINGTON - US President Roosevelt began to study the Far East problem in detail today. Dr. Stuart, President of Yenching University in Peiping, has been ordered by the President to submit his impressions and suggestions regarding Japan's military actions in mainland China within the next few days. It is reported that Dr. Stuart will suggest that Western countries support China with political and economic power to maintain its territorial integrity. Dr. Stuart was summoned to the White House today to express his views on Japan's invasion of mainland China. As a result of the conversation, the President ordered him to submit a written opinion within 24 hours. Afterwards, Dr. Stuart met with reporters and stated that he believed the Sino-Japanese crisis had reached a point where all countries should take joint action. He does not advocate the use of force and believes there is no need for it. Japan's invasion of mainland China is completely without justification and violates not only existing treaties between the two countries, but also the international law protecting law and order. Even if the United States alone were to aid China with political and economic means, he does not see the possibility of triggering a Japanese-American war. It is noted that the US President's sudden study of the Far East problem has caused surprise in the US capital. Outside sources speculate that the conflict on the Manchurian-Russian border also had at least some influence. According to seemingly accurate information received by the US government, the puppet government has threatened Soviet Russia. If Russia does not grant all of the puppet state's demands regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway incident, it will use force. Therefore, the situation is quite serious. Furthermore, Chinese Finance Minister Song Ziwen is about to arrive in the United States. Therefore, the US President is collecting information in advance and summoning Dr. Stuart to seek his opinion. The White House talks this week are scheduled for representatives from Argentina, Italy, Germany, and China.

(1st National Telegram)

(Nanjing) It is heard that the trips of Gu Weijun and Guo Taiqi to Washington have both been cancelled. However, the National Government hopes that at least one of the two will go to the United States by mid-May to assist Finance Minister Song in carrying out all matters. Gu recently telegraphed from Paris, saying that he is suffering from insomnia due to overwork in Geneva and wishes to rest for a while. (1st Reuters Telegram)

(London) Today, Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi met with US President's representative in Europe, Davis, to discuss recent developments in the Far East. Ambassador Guo told Davis that recent rumors that China is willing to negotiate a truce are completely unfounded. China is determined to continue to resist the Japanese invasion. (2nd National News Agency Telegram)

US Government Instructs Davis

To Promote Tariff Truce

(New York) The US government today instructed its representative in London, Davis, to urge the immediate establishment of a tariff truce. Even if it is attached with the reservation that Britain and France have the right to levy additional taxes if the US dollar depreciates, it is still acceptable. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

Dalian Newspaper Publishes

Statistics on Northeastern Anti-Japanese Armies

(Dalian) According to statistics published today by a certain Dalian newspaper, a year ago, there were 230,000 righteous volunteers in the Three Northeastern Provinces. However, only 60,000 remain now. Moreover, the current volunteers are extremely lacking in military supplies and seem to be living by begging. The loss of Jehol has cut off the supply routes. The existing volunteers have all become armed refugees. The volunteers in Heilongjiang were extremely active in the spring and summer of last year, but now there are fewer than 3,000 remaining. There are currently 25,000 volunteers in Jilin Province, making it the province with the most volunteers in the Three Northeastern Provinces. These are mostly subordinates of Wang Delin, Li Du, etc., who have not retreated into Russian territory. The remaining volunteers have moved to Heilongjiang. There are currently 13,000 volunteers in Liaoning Province, mostly located in the Tongping area. There are currently 6,000 volunteers in western Jehol, as well as 10,000 genuine bandits. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

Chinese Eastern Railway Dispute

Russian Aircraft Reconnoiter Border

Russian-Japanese Situation Increasingly Dangerous

Russian General Manager Sends Letter Replying to the Puppet Manchurian Government

Reiterating Ownership of the Chinese Eastern Railway

The Puppet State Resolves to Block Transportation on the Suifen River

Russian Customs Officials on the Border Begin to Withdraw

(Harbin) The Russian-Manchurian dispute over the Chinese Eastern Railway is now becoming increasingly serious. Soviet Russia has announced that it will not return the vehicles that have withdrawn into Russian territory, and Soviet Russian customs officials in Manzhouli and Suifenhe have withdrawn into Russian territory. Soviet Russian aircraft are now extremely active along the border area. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

(Harbin) According to a report from the Manzhouli border guard, two Soviet Russian military aircraft have been flying over the border area in recent days. This is the first time since the Sino-Russian War of 1929 that Russian aircraft have approached the border, which shows the severity of the Russian-Manchurian situation. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

(Moscow) The dispute between Soviet Russia and the puppet organization over the ownership and operation of the Chinese Eastern Railway has intensified today after receiving the puppet organization's formal report denying Soviet Russia's sole ownership. Today, the Soviet Russian government published continued reports on the negotiations between the Russian representative of the railway and the puppet authorities, and claimed that it had instructed the Russian representative to insist on the immediate restoration of normal conditions and to strictly abide by the Beijing and Shenyang agreements. At this time, Soviet Russia is demanding complete ownership of the railway in accordance with the two agreements. Therefore, one of the documents exchanged between the two parties in Harbin, published today, pointed out that Soviet Russia's opening of some locomotives into Russian territory was an illegal unilateral action. However, today the Russian government no longer debated the ownership of the vehicles in the communique, claiming that the Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian agreements explicitly recognize the Chinese Eastern Railway as Soviet Russian property. Therefore, it is stipulated that China can buy back the railway under certain conditions, which is clear evidence that China recognizes that the ownership of the railway belongs to Russia. The "interference of Manchurian officials" is a violation of the treaty. At this time, what the Russian government is demanding is only the immediate conclusion of a technical agreement for the operation of the railway. In addition, the Russian government also stated that if "Manchukuo" makes any further demands regarding the ownership of the railway, Soviet Russia will no longer pay attention to it. (30th National Telegram)

(Moscow) The serious conflict between Soviet Russia and "Manchukuo" shows no sign of being resolved. Li Shaogeng, the puppet director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, sent a letter to the Russian General Manager Kosnitzky, denying that Soviet Russia enjoys ownership of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Kosnitzky replied that Soviet Russian ownership is recorded in the clauses of the two treaties signed in Shenyang and Beiping. Now (Manchukuo) suddenly raises the issue of Soviet Russian ownership, causing people to fear that "Manchukuo's" purpose is to destroy these two treaties. (30th Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) Although Japanese authorities are taking a cold attitude towards the dispute between Soviet Russia and the "puppet state" over the Chinese Eastern Railway and continue to claim that this case will not have major developments, according to reports from Changchun, the authorities there believe that this dispute can only be resolved if Soviet Russia agrees to cancel the 1924 Shenyang Agreement and conclude a new treaty. The new treaty must have equal clauses. The Soviet Russian government's second protest to Changchun accused the "Russian-Manchukuo" of violating the Shenyang Agreement. The "puppet Manchukuo" government claimed that "Manchukuo" had not violated anything, because the agreement was signed by the former government, and the Soviet Russian government took advantage of the weakness of the former government to achieve it. (1st Reuters Telegram)

(Dalian) After Kosnitzky sent the third reply to Li Shaogeng regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway, the "puppet Manchukuo" government decided to block transportation on the Suifen River, causing great tension among the people. Kosnitzky's letter still insisted that the Chinese Eastern Railway belongs to Soviet Russia. The "puppet Manchukuo" government declared that the Soviet Russian reply makes a peaceful resolution impossible. It is also rumored that on April 23, two Soviet Russian aircraft invaded Manchurian territory and flew over Pingyang Town, about fifteen miles from the Russian-Manchurian border. This incident also caused unease among the people. (1st Reuters Telegram)

(Harbin) The Harbin Times, a Japanese-run newspaper, today published a harsh editorial on the Russian-Manchurian Chinese Eastern Railway dispute, stating: "The thieves of the Chinese Eastern Railway and their associates should be held fully responsible for this matter. As for the relationship between Russia and Manchuria, it will depend on the attitude of Soviet Russia." The newspaper also said that the Chinese Eastern Railway does not belong to Soviet Russia, because Karakhan had already briefly stated in his note to China on September 27, 1930 that Soviet Russia was abandoning its ownership of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Therefore, the Chinese Eastern Railway already belongs to China. Now, the Russian Deputy Director Kosnitzky still insists that the Chinese Eastern Railway belongs to Russia, presumably having forgotten Karakhan's previous note. Finally, the newspaper said that the Russian side should quickly return the vehicles of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Currently, in the Chinese Eastern Railway dispute, neither the Russian nor the Manchurian side is willing to concede. Officials are generally pessimistic about this, and Soviet Russia has stopped returning vehicles, even refusing to release freight cars. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

League of Nations Advisory Committee to Decide

On Measures for Non-Recognition of the Puppet State

League of Nations Secretariat Has Distributed Report to All Members

Advisory Committee May Convene This Week

(Geneva) The League of Nations Secretariat has drafted various issues related to the non-recognition of "Manchukuo" and will distribute them to the members of the subcommittee handling the issue. The committee is scheduled to meet at the end of this week to discuss everything. It is heard that the report did not make any suggestions, which is naturally not within the scope of the Secretariat's authority. The report only examines all international relations of non-recognition of "Manchukuo," as this move involves currency, passports, postal and telecommunications, consular status, etc. The subcommittee will submit recommendations to the Twenty-Two Committee, which was appointed by the League of Nations General Assembly to assist in fulfilling its responsibilities. The Twenty-Two Committee may convene this week. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

(London) A certain Japanese advisor to "Manchukuo" recently claimed that those who do not recognize "Manchukuo" cannot enjoy preferential tariffs. A question was therefore raised in the British House of Commons today. Lord President of the Council Baldwin replied on behalf of Foreign Secretary Simon, who was unwell, that the maintenance of the open-door policy in Manchuria is enshrined in the treaty. The comments of a certain advisor obviously contradict the repeated declarations of the Japanese government and the Manchurian authorities. If Japan and Manchuria were to break their declaration of an open door, the British government would take any possible steps to defend this principle. However, he has not received any news of this action by Japan and Manchuria. Given the previous statements of Japan and Manchuria, the words of a certain advisor are difficult to believe. (1st Reuters)

Bandits Still Active in Newchwang

(Dalian) Bandits are still active in Newchwang. Although the authorities speak of suppressing bandits every day, it is ineffective. Recently, there was another case of a certain Chinese businessman being kidnapped. One morning, two people arrived at a certain merchant's house in a car, saying that the court had summoned him. The merchant then went with them. His daughter also went to the door and saw nothing unusual. Unexpectedly, he never returned. It is heard that the merchant was coerced by the bandits and changed to a small boat midway to cross the river, heading towards the bandit den in Panshan. (1st Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Fleet

Rotation in Qinhuangdao

(Tokyo) The 15th Destroyer Squadron, "Fuji," "Tsuta," "Usu," and "Ogi," which were guarding the Shanhaiguan area, departed from Yingkou yesterday to return to Wu on the morning of the 4th, as they were ordered to rotate with the Maizuru Torpedo Squadron. (2nd Denstu Telegram)

Result of Matsudaira's Appeal to England

Britain Proposes to Japan

Holding a London Conference

To Discuss Preventing Trade Competition Between the Two Countries

Japan is Skeptical but Principally Expresses Acceptance

The Turkish-Japanese Commercial Treaty Extended for Three Months

(Tokyo) This morning, the Japanese government received a suggestion from Minister Runciman of the British Board of Trade, relayed by Japanese Ambassador to the United Kingdom Matsudaira, advocating that British and Japanese industrialists hold a conference in London to discuss various commercial matters between Britain and Japan. Japan seems likely to accept this proposal. (1st Reuters Telegram)

(London) Minister Runciman of the Board of Trade, through Japanese Ambassador to the United Kingdom Matsudaira, proposed to Japan the suggestion of a gathering of British and Japanese industrialists in London to discuss commerce between the two countries. People in the Manchester cotton industry are cautiously in favor of this proposal, hoping to improve the position of the British cotton industry, which is severely affected by Japanese goods. There are also those who oppose this proposal, because it is tantamount to admitting Britain's weakness. Opponents advocate raising tariffs on Japanese goods entering the British Empire. The Manchester Royal Exchange approved the request of the Cotton Goods Alliance, and members of the exchange signed a letter to the government requesting a ban on foreign countries expanding their commerce in British Empire markets. This is truly an unprecedented move. The panic in Lancashire can be seen from this. (1st Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) Because the United Kingdom cancelled the Japanese-Indian Commercial Treaty, Matsudaira, the Japanese ambassador to the United Kingdom, contacted the British government authorities several times under the order of Foreign Minister Uchida. Minister Runciman of the British Board of Trade proposed an agreement on markets to the Japanese ambassador. Matsudaira immediately telegraphed the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs for instructions. The outline of the British proposal is as follows: (1) Matters related to the cancellation of the Indian-Japanese Commercial Treaty and the Indian Industries Protection Act should be discussed from a global perspective to find remedies. Partial consultations are of no avail. (2) The United Kingdom wants to use this opportunity to include the area where British and Japanese goods compete in all British territories and world markets as the scope of consultation and jointly study methods of ceasing conflict and forming a comprehensive agreement. (3) To achieve this goal, the British government sincerely hopes that both countries will appoint members, or that industrialists from both countries will organize a joint committee to cease conflict to resolve the economic conflicts between the two countries, agree on markets, and not infringe on their interests. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, upon receiving this report, forwarded it to the Ministry of Commerce and Industry. The Ministry of Commerce and Industry will convene a meeting of representatives from the economic sector to determine countermeasures. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has expressed acceptance of this proposal in principle. (1st China United Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs held a meeting of its leadership to study the British proposal for a British-Japanese Trade Agreement Committee. After exchanging opinions with the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, it expressed its approval in principle of the British proposal. However, there are major questions about the matters that should be discussed by the operators of both countries, such as (1) the scope of the market that should be agreed upon, (2) whether it includes the Indian market, (3) whether the market agreement extends to an agreement on the control of exports and restrictions on production in their own countries, (4) the relationship with tariff agreements, and (5) the scope of commodities applicable to the trade agreement, such as varieties. As details are unknown, they all dare not make trade promises and have telegraphed Ambassador Matsudaira to inquire about the detailed intentions of the British government. (2nd Denstu Telegram)

(Tokyo) Regarding the British Minister's proposal, although the Japanese business community has not discussed it, their opinions and predictions are roughly as follows: (1) Although the British proposal is not a bad way to break the deadlock, it is difficult to predict its intentions, or it may be a trick to avoid discussing Japanese-Indian trade. (2) The problem is currently occurring in India, but the scope of the agreement is the entire British territory and the world cloth market, which proves that the British colonies will adopt an offensive policy towards Japanese goods. No matter how it ends, Japanese goods imported into the British colonies will be affected. (3) The reason why the British included the markets of Southeast Asia and China in the scope of consultation is that they intend to demand that Japanese goods withdraw from British colonies in exchange. Japan has nothing to gain. The Japanese business community said that if the consultation is not done properly, it may cause a full-scale conflict between Britain and Japan. Therefore, the Japanese side should carefully study countermeasures. (2nd China United Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Turkish-Japanese Provisional Commercial Agreement will expire on the 6th. According to a telegram from Murakami, the acting ambassador to Turkey, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Turkey and Japan have extended the validity of the provisional agreement by three months to avoid being a country without a treaty. During that time it will remain in effect, with an unofficial understanding having been reached. (2nd Denstu Telegram)

Japanese Anti-British Movement

Slogans Pasted All Over Tokyo

Bitterly Denouncing British Anti-Japanism

(Tokyo) Recently, anti-British slogans printed in black, white, and red characters have been pasted on wooden signs, bamboo fences, and telephone poles all over Tokyo. Among them, the black background with large white characters is posted by an organization calling itself the Asia-British United Association. Most of them criticize Britain for disregarding British-Japanese friendship, repaying kindness with ingratitude, forcing Japan to accept an inappropriate naval ratio at the Washington Conference, and encouraging anti-Japanese sentiment in Geneva, and demanding the liberation of India to free it from the yoke of British rule, and gathering 400 million Chinese people and 300 million Indian people to drive British forces west of the Suez Canal. (1st Reuters Telegram)

Page 9

Soviet Russian Ambassador Presents Credentials

Chairman Lin Holds a Lavish Banquet

Russian Ambassador to Host Journalists Tomorrow

(Nanjing) Russian Ambassador Bogomolov presented his credentials on the morning of the 2nd. This is the first time since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing that an ambassador has presented credentials in the capacity of ambassador. On the morning of the 2nd, the ambassador went from the Yangtze River Hotel in Xiaguan to the National Government. The police and military guarded both sides of the street. Zhang Xiqian, Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies, welcomed the Russian ambassador to the National Government. The car he was riding in was the No. 1 black limousine in Nanjing. The Russian ambassador and his staff were all dressed in black formal attire. Chairman Lin and Foreign Minister Luo were dressed in Chinese formal attire, a blue robe, a black mandarin jacket, and leather boots. At noon, Chairman Lin held a banquet at the National Government to entertain the Russian ambassador and his staff. The heads of the five Yuan, Foreign Minister Luo, the two Chiefs of Civilian Staff and Military Staff, and others were in attendance. The banquet was very lavish, with three roast pigs. It is also the first time that the Chairman of the National Government has formally entertained foreign guests. The banquet ended at around 2:00 PM. Zhang Xiqian and Liu Difan accompanied the Russian ambassador back to the guesthouse. Foreign Minister Luo changed the date to the evening of the 4th to entertain the Russian ambassador. The Russian ambassador is scheduled to host the press at 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 4th. Reporters from various newspapers visited on the 2nd, but were not received. The location of the embassy has not yet been determined. It will probably be chosen from two locations, Dafang Lane and Changfu Street, for temporary use, and then construction will be carried out. The Russian ambassador will not leave Nanjing within ten days and will discuss various issues with our diplomatic authorities. (2nd Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov presented his credentials at 11:30 AM on the morning of the 2nd. The National Government first sent Zhang Xiqian, Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies, and Liu Naifan, Section Chief, to the Yangtze River Hotel to welcome him. Military and police were stationed along the way to salute. The Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies entered to report after the ambassador arrived at the government. The Chairman came to the auditorium in formal attire and stood in the center. The Chief of Civilian Staff and the Chief of Military Staff led all the civilian staff and military staff, dividing into east and west sides. The Foreign Minister and translators stood to the right of the Chairman. The Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies invited the ambassador to enter the audience. The ambassador entered the auditorium and the audience was held as scheduled. The Chairman returned the salutes one by one. After the ambassador delivered his eulogy, it was translated into Chinese by Chinese Secretary E Shanyin for the Chairman. After the translation, the ambassador presented his credentials. The Chairman received them and handed them to the Foreign Minister, who read the reply, which was translated by Sun Guanghua. After reading, the Chairman shook hands with the ambassador and chatted, asking about the health of the Chairman of the Soviet Republic for a moment. The ambassador then went to see the members of each embassy and shook hands with them one by one. After the ambassador stood at attention and bowed to the Chairman, he retreated step by step as scheduled. The Chairman returned the salutes one by one. The ambassador and his staff exited the auditorium and re-entered the reception room. The Foreign Minister and the two Chiefs of Civilian and Military Staff also entered the reception room to socialize with the ambassador, and served wine and snacks. After the Chairman returned to his office to rest, he came to the reception room and stayed with the ambassador until entering the banquet room to take a seat. The ministers of each Yuan, the two Chiefs of Civilian and Military Staff of the National Government, the Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies, Foreign Vice Minister Xu Mo, and Councilor Zhang and Section Chief Zhu, etc., took their seats in order. After the banquet, the Chairman and the ambassador, as well as the members in attendance, took a photo and returned to the reception room. The ambassador shook hands with the Chairman and bid farewell, and was accompanied back to the ambassador's guesthouse in a limousine by the welcoming staff. (2nd Central News Agency Telegram)

Roosevelt to Attend as a Guest

At the World Economic Conference

Formal Decision on Japanese Representative Candidates

Six-Province Joint Conference Formulates Guiding Principles

(New York) According to a Washington visitor today, President Roosevelt may attend the World Economic Conference to be held in London in mid-June, but the President will only attend as a guest, not as a representative of the United States. He plans to invite former Ohio Governor Cox to join the US delegation attending the World Economic Conference and has specially asked for his consent. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) This morning's cabinet meeting formally approved the dispatch of Ishii, Matsudaira, and Fukai as Japanese representatives to the World Economic Conference. Afterwards, Matsuoka reported on the beginning and end of attending the League of Nations meeting to pass the Lytton Report. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government's countermeasures for the World Economic Conference were formulated in the original draft at the six-province joint conference on the 1st and have been approved by the cabinet. The content is divided into two parts: the first part is the countermeasures for the London Conference, and the second part is the countermeasures for the Washington Conference, to abolish the extreme policy. The content is described as follows: (A) "Countermeasures for the London Conference" (1) (Monetary and Credit Policy) Before restoring the gold standard, the freedom of capital movement must be resolved first. The gold standard issue must be resolved in connection with the country's credit. Credit policy should adopt the cooperation of central banks of various countries. As for raising the price of silver to increase the purchasing power of the Far East market, it is a method that Japan desperately desires. The silver issue is about stability, not price increases. (2) (Price Policy) Japan's national conditions require high prices. Within the scope that can accommodate Japan's special circumstances, Japan is willing to accept world control. (3) (Capital Movement) Reopening the path of capital movement includes various methods such as canceling restrictions on exchange, changing short-term national debt to long-term debt, and using the Bank for International Settlements. However, Japan advocates free passage as a basic countermeasure. (4) (International Trade) Cancel all kinds of restrictions on national defense trade, but rice is not governed by this principle. (5) (Tariffs and Commercial Treaties) Free trade and tariff barrier reductions are new trade principles, but Japan is unwilling to reduce its tariffs equally with other countries. (6) (Production and Transactions) Restrictions on production and export should be free to each country, without any international pressure. (B) "Countermeasures for the Washington Conference" (1) Japan cancels its extreme policy on any issue that restricts Japanese national policy. (2) Regarding the Far East issue and the Manchurian issue, actively seek American understanding. (3) When all resolutions reach the final voting stage, strive for Japan's unique circumstances. If understanding cannot be reached, then agree with conditions. (4) Military disarmament opposes the same degree of reduction as other countries for reasons of Far Eastern political affairs. (5) Matters that have already been agreed upon between the United States and the United States, if they do not violate Japan's stated special circumstances, need not be opposed. (China United Telegram)

Xiao's Troops Threaten the Enemy's Flank

(Beiping) Regarding Xinglong, on the 29th, about four or five hundred enemy troops advancing westward from Jinshanzi towards Keli Village engaged in fierce battle for three hours with our Xiao's troops at the highlands northwest of Tucheng Head. Fortunately, our troops stationed at Huangtuliang heard the sounds and advanced eastward, threatening the enemy's flank. The enemy was unable to withstand the attack and collapsed, retreating towards Yingshou Camp. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy Artillery Test-Fires at Our Positions

(Beiping) Miyun telegram: On the 1st, the enemy continuously used artillery to fire at our positions, seemingly as a test. On the 30th night, the enemy dispatched a unit of about two hundred soldiers to attack our positions, but they retreated after our resistance. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Only Outpost Contact at the Front Lines

(Nanchang) Miyun telegram: At Gubeikou, the enemy's gunfire on the 30th night was incessant, and they frequently used searchlights to illuminate our side. They were also quite busy transporting various materials forward, appearing to be constructing solid fortifications there. There was only contact between outposts and sentries at the front lines. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy's Fierce Assault on Xinglong Fails

(Beiping) Xiao Zhichu's telegram from the 30th to Beiping: Early on the 30th, a mixed Japanese-Manchu force of about seven or eight hundred soldiers, and another two hundred or so in the Shouwangfen area, launched several fierce attacks on our Xinglong positions in an attempt to relieve the siege. Our brigade fought back fiercely, killing over two hundred enemy soldiers. The enemy has completely collapsed and retreated in a panic towards the northeast. Our army suffered slight casualties. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy Aircraft Drop Bombs on Xinglong County

(Beiping) Several enemy aircraft circled over Xinglong from morning until noon, dropping over two hundred bombs, completely destroying civilian houses. Over ten of our officers and soldiers were wounded or killed. We are currently continuing to pursue and suppress [the enemy]. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy Attack on Chedao Ridge Repelled

(Beiping) Miyun telegram: Yesterday at around 11 PM, the enemy bombarded our Nantianmen positions with artillery, firing approximately a hundred shells. This morning at around 2 AM, the enemy again used two to three hundred infantry soldiers to launch a sneak attack on our Bijia Mountain positions from Yangzhuang Heilongtan, but they were repelled by our defending soldiers. At dawn today, about two hundred enemy soldiers again advanced towards Chedao Ridge, but they were also repelled by our defending soldiers. The enemy has built solid fortifications at Huangtuliang and is currently confronting our army. The enemy's highest-ranking commander is stationed in the Liang Xiuting residence north of the Laoye Temple in Gubeikou. A machine gun emplacement has been established on the north bank of the Chao River. In recent days, over five thousand Mongol-Korean cavalry have arrived from Luanping. A portion of the Japanese troops is retreating towards Chengde, the reason is unknown. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Three Traitors Captured in Shixia

(Beiping) The enemy has been sending traitors to scout behind our lines for days. Three have already been captured in Shixia and are currently being strictly interrogated. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Xinglong County Government Building Completely Burned Down

(Beiping) After our army recaptured Xinglong County on the 27th of last month, over a hundred remaining enemy soldiers stubbornly resisted in the Xinglong County government building. On the 29th night, taking advantage of the wind, they completely burned down the county government building. The enemy suddenly lost their foothold and hid in the caves in the backyard of the government building. Our army piled firewood at the cave entrances, poured in petroleum, and set it on fire. The entire enemy army was reduced to ashes. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Certain High-Ranking General Arrives in Beiping

(Beiping) A certain high-ranking general from the front lines of Gubeikou arrived in Beiping this morning to report the situation at the front to He Yingqin and seek instructions. He then went to the Peking Union Medical College Hospital for a medical examination and is scheduled to leave Beiping tonight to return to the front lines to command military affairs. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy Forces on the Gubeikou Front

(Beiping) Miyun telegram: In this battle at Gubeikou, the enemy's main forces consist of the entire Kawahara 16th Brigade and the entire Nakamura 30th Brigade, as well as the 8th Field Artillery Regiment, the 4th Battalion of the Garrison Field Artillery Regiment, the Heavy Artillery Battalion of the 8th Division, the Manchurian 3rd Mountain Artillery Battalion, and various communications units, etc. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Our Army Advances Eastward Along the Beining Railway Line

Minor Contact at Beidaihe Jianchangying

Japanese Troops Destroy Railway West of Qinhuangdao Island

Over a Thousand Puppet Troops Still in the Shenhebao Haiyangzhen Area

(Beiping) Luanzhou telegram: About seven hundred Japanese troops have been discovered near the Tai Touying area of Bohezhai, with plans to advance towards Shutouying Jianchangying. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) On the Beining Railway line, several Japanese armored vehicles and fifty to sixty Japanese infantry and cavalry troops are still stationed in Haiyangzhen. A large number of Japanese and puppet troops still occupy villages northeast of Beidaihe. According to Tianjin news, the Japanese troops are preparing to retreat to the east bank of the Shi River. Our army has advanced to Changli City, Lengkou, Xifengkou and other places. Japanese troops are still holding the area near the passes, confronting our advancing troops. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Last night, over two thousand Japanese and puppet troops were discovered five miles north of Beidaihe, with a small unit probing towards Beidaihe. They were discovered by our Liu Regiment, resulting in a fierce battle. They were repelled at 5 PM on the 2nd. Currently, our Liu Regiment is stationed in Beidaihe. Five or six Japanese warships are stationed in the waters off Qinhuangdao Island, patrolling back and forth. A small squad of Japanese military police is stationed at the Qinhuangdao Island train station. Stores in the Liushouying area of Beidaihe have not opened, and the situation is panicked. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Luanxian telegram: Our armored train No. was ordered this morning to advance from Beidaihe Station to Nandasi and Qinhuangdao. The bridge [words missing] Yinma River and Beidaihe has been repaired and is fully intact. A certain regiment is currently guarding Liushouying. The division advancing from Changli is gradually advancing along the railway line towards Beidaihe and Qinhuangdao this morning. There are over a thousand puppet troops and dozens of Japanese troops in the Shenhebao Haiyangzhen area, with a total of over thirty armored vehicles. The puppet troops launched a counterattack against Liushouying the night before last but were repelled by our regiment. The Japanese and puppet troops appear to be retreating towards Liujiang. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Luanzhou, 2nd: There was no fighting in eastern Luanzhou. Our front line is now at Beidaihe, confronting the enemy at Mafang north of Beidaihe. He Zhuguo inspected eastern Luanzhou this morning and comforted the soldiers and civilians along the way. He returned to Luanzhou from Beidaihe in the evening. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Enemy and Traitors in Eastern Luanzhou Counterattack Again

(Tianjin) The enemy and traitors in eastern Luanzhou, discovering that our army had changed its defenses, launched a counterattack again. There was fighting on the 1st between Beidaihe and the northern area and Qian'an Jianchangying. Passenger trains on the Beining Railway still run to Changli on the 1st. The railway bridge east of Liushouying has not yet been repaired. The situation in that area is becoming serious again. It will be difficult to realize the opening of the railway to Qinhuangdao within a few days. (1st, Special Dispatch)

Enemy Surrounded Near Taolin Camp

(Beiping) Luanzhou telegram: The enemy near Jianchangying launched an attack from Taolin Camp on our positions near Lulong, with puppet troops as the vanguard. Our Weng Zhaoyuan's troops dispatched a unit to encircle the enemy. They surrounded the enemy near Taolin Camp. After a long and fierce battle, they finally repelled the enemy, captured over thirty puppet soldiers alive, and seized a large number of weapons. The enemy and puppet troops retreated towards Jianchangying. For days, the enemy has been using puppet troops to launch sneak attacks on our positions, but all have failed. The main force of the puppet troops along the railway line is still gathered in the Haiyangzhen area. They are confronting our Liu troops in Fanjadian Houmafang. Our army is sending cavalry to attack towards the Tang River bank. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Two Enemy Armored Trains Arrive in Qinhuangdao

(Beiping) Train No. 102 on the Beining Railway was four hours late, only arriving in Beiping at 2 PM today. At 2 PM on the 1st, two enemy armored trains suddenly arrived in Qinhuangdao, carrying over three hundred soldiers. One train opened fire at Nandasi, firing at our front lines to prevent us from repairing the railway bridge there, and exchanged fire with our Liu troops sentries, preventing our repairs. It then retreated. The reason for the enemy's reinforcement of Qinhuangdao this time is to cover the retreat of puppet troops who have not yet been completely evacuated from Funing and other places, and to prevent our army from pursuing them. There is no sign of a westward advance. Train No. 7 on the Beining Railway is still running to Liushouying and Beidaihe. The railway to Qinhuangdao can be opened within a few days. It is heard that the Japanese army's retreat plan will ultimately stop at Shanhaiguan. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Opening of the Railway to Qinhuangdao Hopeless in the Near Future

The puppet troops near Beidaihe in Luanzhou, after being fiercely attacked by our reinforced cavalry on the night of the 30th, have retreated in disarray towards the northeast. Since the morning of the 1st, the enemy has been constructing fortifications near Nandasi and the villages in the Zhangjia Mafang area. On the 1st, between Nandasi and Zhangjia Mafang southwest of Qinhuangdao, there were over ten Japanese soldiers and two hundred and seventy puppet soldiers supervising railway workers to destroy the railway. It is feared that the opening of the railway to Qinhuangdao is hopeless in the near future. (1st, Special Dispatch)

Duolun Has Been Lost

Japanese Troops Rush to Duolun

Our Front Line is in the Liutang Area

(Beiping) Tang Yulin and Feng Zhanhai sent a telegram from the east yesterday, stating that enemies have been discovered in Duolun and were in contact with our Zhao Chengzhou's cavalry stationed in Duolun. Zhao's troops withdrew from Duolun on the evening of the 29th. Friendly troops stationed in Duolun and local administrative personnel also withdrew to Guyuan that evening. On the morning of the 29th, the Red Swastika Society in Duolun City reported, requesting that cars be sent to Duolun to transport wounded soldiers as soon as possible. Since the morning of the 1st, telegrams between Duolun and Guyuan have been cut off. Our army is currently on strict alert, determined to fiercely attack the enemy when they come. Two weeks ago, there were already reports of enemy troops harassing Duolun, and the people fled. From time to time, Mongolian bandits, under the direction of the Japanese, calling themselves the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army, appeared near Duolun and attacked our army. Duolun has been lost, and there are no defenses. Only Zhangbei County, ninety miles from Zhangjiakou, can be used for resistance. Sun Dianying telegraphed on the 27th that the enemy who arrived at Banjietou from Chuizishan on the 19th was the bandit army of Liu Guitang and two Japanese cavalry battalions, with eight armored vehicles, totaling about ten thousand people. Liu himself outwardly expressed his allegiance, but is actually preparing to attack Chahar. It is heard that the Japanese have appointed Liu as the commander-in-chief of the attack on Chahar, and promised him the governorship of Chahar Province. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Feng Zhanhai telegraphed to Beiping, stating that our army abandoned Duolun on the 29th and is building new positions northeast of Bianqiangzi, reorganizing its ranks, and reversing the political situation towards the enemy. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Feng Zhanhai telegraphed, stating that the cavalry and infantry previously sent to a certain place encountered puppet troops and Mongolian bandits on the way, and engaged in a fierce battle for eight hours. They repelled the puppet troops, killing over twenty enemy soldiers, capturing twelve prisoners, and seizing seventeen guns. Our army suffered one wounded company commander, Zhao Fuchang, and thirteen soldiers, who were sent to Zhangjiakou for treatment. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Military Council stated that it has not received an official report from the front regarding the fall of Duolun as of this morning. Based on their assumptions, the loss may be a fact. However, the enemies entering eastern Chahar are all puppet troops and Mongolian bandits. The majority of the Japanese army has not advanced, and even if they have, it is only a very small number. Feng Zhanhai's troops are currently reorganizing in a certain place southwest of the area. Zhao Chengzhou has led his troops along the highway, retreating towards the area. The distance between the stationing places of Feng Zhanhai's troops and Duolun is considerable. A counter-attack seems to still require preparation. The situation in Zhangjiakou is extremely tense. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) With the fall of Duolun and Zhangjiakou under pressure, rumors are rife in the area. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) It is reported that Song Zheyuan arrived in Beiping from Zhangjiakou last night and will visit He Yingqin tonight to report on the situation in eastern Chahar and discuss defense matters. He will return to Zhangjiakou within a few days. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) The news of the fall of Duolun has spread and officials and civilians are shaken. The Suiyuan Pacification Headquarters is seriously discussing measures. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A person from Zhangjiakou said that Feng Yuxiang, due to the Japanese army's invasion of eastern Chahar and the tense situation, summoned his guards and engineers on the 30th, instructing them to prepare their broadswords and prepare to fight the enemy to the death. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Sun Dianying was ordered to concentrate his troops in a certain place near Kangzhuang, threatening the enemy's flank. Sun's advance troop, the Ding Brigade, was ordered on the 1st to advance from its stationing place to a certain place. Sun Dianying is still in Chicheng. There was heavy snow all day yesterday morning, and the climate is extremely cold. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Guyuan telegram: The rebel troops of Liu Guitang and Cui Xingwu had a conflict over pay and weapons on the afternoon of the 30th, and a portion of Cui's army was eliminated. The Japanese side has recently urgently transferred the 39th Division and the 49th Field Heavy Artillery Regiment from western Rehe to Duolun. Japanese aircraft have been traveling between Chengde and Duolun for days, transporting military supplies. Over a hundred of our wounded soldiers in Duolun were unable to retreat in time and were all killed. Tang is still in Guyuan, and the entire 5th and 15th Armies of his troops are concentrated in Guyuan and Shangzhuang counties. Our front line is in the Liutang area, and the defenses are solid. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Uprising Occurs in Shenyang

(Tokyo) News received here states that an uprising occurred in Shenyang on Sunday. Seventy security guards, recently returned from the Rehe battlefield, attacked a police station near the East Gate, but were disarmed by the police and Japanese soldiers. There was no bloodshed. Another report said that two Japanese police officers stopped a car driven by five military police officers. The military police officers refused to comply and attempted to disarm the Japanese police officers, but were severely beaten by the Japanese police officers. The military police officers ran back to their camp for help. The entire military police force left the camp and went directly to the East Gate Police Station, helping the rioters of about a hundred people, and began to attack, but they were driven back. The military police officers then gathered about two hundred people and attacked again, seizing weapons from the station and beating a police officer. Shortly after, Japanese soldiers and police drove back the crowd and arrested seventy people. (2nd, Reuters Dispatch)

Chiang Summons Representatives of Sichuan Army

Instructs on Policies for Stabilizing Sichuan Situation

And Orders All Armies to Unite in Suppressing Bandits

Zhang Qun Returns to Nanjing for In-Depth Discussions with the Central Government

(Nanjing) Representatives of the Sichuan armies stationed in Nanjing, having previously been summoned to Jiangxi by Chiang's telegram, instructed on policies for stabilizing the Sichuan situation and suppressing bandits. The representatives immediately telegraphed the Sichuan army authorities to report the intentions of Chiang on Sichuan matters and jointly returned to Nanjing on the 2nd. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, Tang Youren, has returned to Nanjing from Jiangxi. According to him, the Jiangxi bandits have gradually become impoverished since Chiang Kai-shek personally supervised the armies to encircle and suppress them. They are expected to be eliminated in the shortest period of time. Chiang is extremely busy in Nanchang, planning military affairs for the suppression of bandits, and will not leave Jiangxi in the next few days. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Zhang Qun has returned to Nanjing from Jiangxi. He will have in-depth discussions with the Central Government regarding methods for reorganizing Sichuan. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) The bandit suppression conference of Sichuan army representatives in Nanchang closed on the 30th. Chiang instructed all armies to unite in suppressing bandits and not allow them to spread, as Jiangxi is beyond redemption. He also ordered each to send military commissioners to Nanchang to inspect the bandit situation at the front lines and understand the advantages and disadvantages. No other matters were decided. The representatives have returned to Nanjing and Hankou. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Tian Songyao telegraphed Hankou on the 1st, stating that his troops launched a full-scale general offensive against Xu's bandits on the 26th, and the bandits have been shaken by the 30th. The Wan Brigade captured He Bajia Ping, the Liu Division occupied Heiyan, the Zeng Brigade occupied Wulong Di Chen Jia Ba, the Xie Brigade occupied Ma Jia Ping, and the Li Department occupied Desheng Mountain. The Zeng Division occupied Yinggezui and is now attacking Tongjiang, which can be captured soon. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Chiang convened a conference on bandit suppression in Sichuan in Nanchang. It is heard that it has closed. All armies must dispatch troops to assist in the suppression in accordance with the resolutions, with the number determined by the distance of the stationed location. Regarding the issue of sending troops to resist Japan, it is heard that only preliminary preparations can be made, and mobilization can only occur when supplies are available. (1st, Special Dispatch)

Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, Hubei

Three Bandit Suppression Commanders-in-Chief

Have Been Officially Appointed by the National Government

Chen Jitang, He Jian, Liu Zhi

(Nanjing) The National Government issued an order on the 1st, specially appointing Chen Jitang as the Commander-in-Chief of the Southern Route of the Bandit Suppression Army in Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei, Bai Chongxi as the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Southern Route, Cai Tingkai as the Front-Line Commander-in-Chief of the Southern Route, He Jian as the Commander-in-Chief of the Western Route, Liu Zhi as the Commander-in-Chief of the Northern Route, and Liu Zhenhua as the Commander-in-Chief of the Bandit Suppression Army in the Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Border Region. (1st, Central News Agency)

National Government

Issues Decree to Comfort the People of Xinjiang

Jin Shuren Approved to be Relieved of All Concurrent Positions

Huang Musong Has Arrived in Nanjing and is Preparing to Depart for Xinjiang

(Nanjing) The National Government ordered on the 2nd that the application for resignation submitted by Jin Shuren, the Chairman of the Xinjiang Provincial Government, concurrently the Border Defense Commissioner of Xinjiang, be approved, and Jin Shuren be relieved of all concurrent positions. He is ordered to come to Nanjing immediately and await further appointment.

The order further stated that national equality and freedom of religion are the basic tenets of our Party and the essential principles of the Provisional Constitution. The National Government has consistently adhered to these principles in its governance of the border provinces. Xinjiang, located in the remote western region, suffers from poor transportation, making communication with the Central Government difficult and preventing the people's concerns from being fully conveyed. However, the Muslim and other peoples of the province are known to the Central Government for their sincerity, honesty, law-abiding nature, and diligence. In recent years, the country has faced many difficulties, and we have not had time to look westward. The people of Xinjiang have been able to maintain their patriotic enthusiasm, understand the government's hardships, and work diligently, contributing greatly to the prosperity of the Republic of China and the unity of the nation. The Central Government has always instructed the border officials to diligently seek the people's concerns and consolidate the border areas. Unexpectedly, since taking office, the Chairman of the province, Jin Shuren, has failed to uphold the intentions of the Central Government in all his actions, leading to this incident, which is deeply regrettable. Now that Chairman Jin Shuren has resigned to take responsibility, the Central Government has approved it and is carefully selecting virtuous individuals to properly manage the area, and has specially appointed Huang Musong, the Vice Chief of Staff of the General Staff Headquarters, as the Xinjiang Envoy to pacify the people, improve the local area, and settle the soldiers and civilians. It is hoped that the people of Xinjiang will understand this intention, abide by their occupations, wait quietly for the process, and not gather in crowds to cause hidden worries. This is our great hope. (2nd, Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) Huang Musong, due to his appointment as the Xinjiang Envoy, went to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang and seek instructions on all plans. He has returned to Nanjing on the 2nd and will meet with Premier Wang and other important figures in Nanjing to discuss measures for handling the Xinjiang incident and report on his experience in Jiangxi. All parties in Xinjiang have expressed their welcome to Huang's visit to Xinjiang. He will depart in a few days. The candidates to be assigned by the relevant agencies to accompany Huang to Xinjiang are being selected. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Su Bingwen's troops and their Secretary-General He Shengda have sent telegrams to Beiping, stating that the army has been ordered to maintain security in Xinjiang. Su has been giving lectures on the China-Japan problem in Dezhou for days. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Lanzhou telegram: Ma Zhongying went to Yumenguan to inspect the border defense, leaving Zhongjie to guard Ruoshui. Two brigades of the 36th Division have left Jiayuguan. Ma stated that the Central Government agreed to the people's request to send Huang Musong to Xinjiang to pacify the region and handle the matter fairly, hoping for a peaceful solution. His troops will never be ordered to enter Xinjiang. Bandits have disappeared from the Lanzhou-Pingliang Highway. The Lanzhou Garrison Commander's office has been officially abolished. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan resolved on the 2nd that the affairs of the Xinjiang Provincial Government will be temporarily maintained by the commissioners and department heads of the Provincial Government. Premier Wang sent a telegram order to the commissioners and department heads of the Provincial Government to inform them of the following: "All commissioners and department heads of the Xinjiang Provincial Government are hereby informed. Recently, due to the incident in Xinjiang, Chairman Jin Shuren has resigned to take responsibility and his resignation has been approved. The Central Government is now carefully selecting virtuous individuals to diligently manage the region. Please work together to maintain the affairs of the Provincial Government, pacify the soldiers and civilians, and improve the local area. This is of utmost importance. Premier of the Executive Yuan, Wang Zhaoming (Winter)". (2nd, Central News Agency)

Cai Tingkai Arrives in Guangzhou

Li Zongren Arrives in Nanchang

(Hong Kong) Cai Tingkai returned to Guangdong on the 2nd and is scheduled to go to Yuanyuantan on the 3rd with Zhang Yantan Qixiu to take an oath. All troops will depart through northern Hunan on the 5th. The Gui army of Tan Lianfang will also depart directly to Hunan to meet up. Deng Longguang's army of Guangdong will depart after the 19th Route Army arrives in a certain place and will meet up in a certain place, all under the control of Cai Tingkai. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

He Chengjun Meets with Various Generals

Instructs on Bandit Suppression Tactics

(Hankou) He Chengjun, upon Chiang's order, will supervise the suppression of the remaining bandits in eastern and western Hubei and has decided to be stationed in Hankou. On the 1st, he met with various generals including Xu Yuanquan, Hao Mengling, Shangguan Yunxiang, and Liang Guanying, who came to Hankou from Xinyang, and instructed them on tactics. Liu Zhenhua will also come to Hankou to visit He and make a final decision on suppressing the bandits in the Henan-Hubei border area. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) He Chengjun has summoned various generals from southern Hubei to Hankou to hold a bandit suppression conference. They are expected to arrive in full force within a few days. It is heard that Liu Zhenhua's troops will be transferred to southern Hubei for bandit suppression. Liu is expected to arrive in Hankou on the evening of the 1st or the morning of the 2nd. (1st, Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) He Chengjun has submitted a report to Chiang and approved that a unit of elite troops will be drawn from a certain province to come to Hubei to assist in the suppression. They are expected to arrive within a short period of time. The troops originally stationed in various subordinate regions will also undergo some changes. He will begin his inspection after the arrangements are in place. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) He Chengjun telegraphed Beiping, stating that he had received an order from the Commander-in-Chief to supervise all units in clearing and suppressing the remaining bandits in various border areas of Hubei Province, which is being implemented separately, aiming to completely eliminate them overnight in the shortest period of time. He will not go north for the time being. (2nd, Special Dispatch)

Jiangxi Bandits Forced to Retreat and Flee

(Nanchang) Military news: The main force of the pseudo-1st Corps, with over ten thousand people, fled to the Zhubei area of Xuanhua County on the 1st. The pseudo-3rd Corps fled to Xianxi, and the pseudo-5th Corps fled to Fuzhang. Our Air Force has been tracking and bombing them. The Zhu bandit headquarters has moved to Gukang. The pseudo-Central Government and important institutions such as the mint and arsenal, due to pressure from the Fujian army and aircraft bombings, have now moved to a small village northwest of Ruijin. (1st, Central News Agency)

Suiyuan Bandits Invade Northern Shaanxi

Guide Fort Near Yulin is Occupied

(Taiyuan) A small unit of the Suiyuan bandit Yang Lin, numbering three thousand, has invaded northern Shaanxi and occupied Guide Fort, forty miles from Yulin. Jing Yuexiu is still in Taiyuan. The commander of his Liu Brigade telegraphed Jing for instructions. Jing ordered the Gao Shuangcheng Brigade to encircle and suppress them. (1st, Special Dispatch)

Current Commentary

閩浙邊境匪勢猖獗

(Fuzhou) The Pacification Headquarters, due to the rampant banditry on the Fujian-Zhejiang border, telegraphed Zhejiang and Shandong to order Qingtai's defense forces to jointly suppress [the bandits]. (2nd Day Special Dispatch)

May Day

The World in All Its Forms

Moscow Holds a Grand Military Parade

Right and Left Wings in Japan Hold Separate Marches and Demonstrations

Germany Changes to "Reconstruction Day" for Enthusiastic Celebrations

Russia

Reuters, Moscow, 1st - Under the red sun today, the grandest military parade in Soviet Russian history was held to celebrate May Day. Over 350 airplanes soared through the sky, and thousands of fast tanks sped across the vast square. Stalin and other leaders stood on the podium next to Lenin's Mausoleum, and 50,000 soldiers cheered as they passed the podium. Stalin wore an olive-green suit and smoked a pipe. Ambassadors from various countries attended the ceremony, except for the British Ambassador. The ceremony lasted two and a half hours before dispersing. Tens of thousands of workers then marched into the square, waving flags without any anti-British slogans.

TASS, Moscow, 1st - Today, this area celebrated "May First" with joyful and enthusiastic ceremonies. Preparations made several days in advance transformed Moscow into a jubilant city. Banners, flags, and charts illustrating industrial progress were hung throughout the streets and squares. Models of machinery and industrial buildings were displayed in Red Square. At precisely 10 a.m., the military parade began in Red Square, led by the Military Commissar Voroshilov. The Red Army and the armaments contingent marched in formation, with large squadrons of aircraft circling above. Stalin, Molotov, Kalinin, and other important party and government officials received cheers of congratulations from the masses as they ascended the Lenin Mausoleum. The entire diplomatic corps attended the ceremony. After Voroshilov's speech, young soldiers took an oath. Large groups of workers marched ahead of the troops, carrying flags celebrating the success of the revolution. This grand ceremony continued until after dusk, with crowds singing songs expressing their belief in the revolution and demanding its ultimate success, filling the entire city.

Germany

Reuters, London, 1st - This year's May Day celebration in Berlin will be more lively than ever before. A million people will participate in parades, and there will be a grand fireworks display. Hitler will then deliver a one-hour speech, broadcast to the public through hundreds of loudspeakers. The first part of Hitler's speech will announce Germany's four-year reconstruction plan, and the second part will address the Nazi Party's purge plan and a grand industrial program.

Havas, Berlin, 2nd - When Berlin celebrated the May Day commemoration, a grand fireworks display was performed at the Tempelhof training ground. The training ground was divided into eight areas, and 200 rockets were launched simultaneously, illuminating the sky like daylight. The fireworks spelled out the letters "Today is Germany's Reconstruction Day," surrounded by lace-like patterns. Then, with a crackling sound, the fireworks changed to another pattern, and the words "Germany is Reconstructed" appeared in the sky. The crowds then returned to the city, saluting various patriotic organizations along the way. Aviation Minister and Prussian Prime Minister Goering delivered a speech to the Nazi stormtroopers at midnight, mainly opposing the disorganization of Germany over the past fifteen years. He advocated uniting all classes of Germany with discipline and friendship. He also said that the government is determined to assist labor, regardless of social class, and finally asked the masses to pledge to trust Germany and fight for Germany. The crowd then sang the German national anthem and dispersed.

Japan

Reuters, Tokyo, 1st - May Day passed quietly. No incidents occurred in major cities such as Tokyo, Osaka, and Yokohama. Although there were many parades today, they all expressed patriotic sentiments rather than labor demonstrations. In the morning, 5,000 right-wing laborers paraded through the city. In the afternoon, 2-3,000 left-wing laborers began to parade.

America

National News, New York, 1st - Radicals in various parts of the United States carried out May Day demonstrations as usual today, but as of tonight, there have been no injuries, and even the damage is extremely minimal. The Socialist Party and the Communist Party of New York held separate parades under police protection without any incidents. In Chicago, five bombs exploded, but the damage was very minor, and there were no serious injuries. The police were able to control the parades. The flag-protesting incidents in the San Francisco parade were more frequent than elsewhere.

France

Havas, Paris, 1st - As May Day began, the whole of France was quiet. The atmosphere in Paris was slightly excited, somewhat like a normal holiday. Buses and trams ran as usual, but there were very few commercial vehicles on the streets. There were no disruptions to public services. Metal factories followed the usual practice of shutting down, and almost all construction workers went on strike. The trade unions only ordered workers to participate in government-approved gatherings. 15,000 communists held a demonstration in the Bois de Vincennes without any incidents. Reports from major cities in the provinces also indicated peace. In some places, communist groups were dispersed by the police. Only in the industrial center of Lille in the north did the communists incite trouble, and there were two clashes, but they did not have much impact. There was no complete shutdown anywhere in France. In many places, work continued as usual. As of 7:30 p.m., the Ministry of Interior reported that the situation throughout the country was unusually peaceful.

Belgium

National News, Brussels, 1st - Today, many members of the Socialist Party held a demonstration in front of the German Consulate, even tearing down the German swastika flag. The police protecting the consulate were overwhelmed by the crowd and could do nothing. Danish socialist crowds stacked themselves into a human pyramid, reaching up and removing the German party symbol. Police reinforcements arrived and dispersed the crowd. The German consulate was not invaded, but the streets and second-floor windows were destroyed by the rioters. The German ambassador to Belgium has lodged a serious protest with the Belgian authorities. The Belgian government has expressed its apologies and promised severe punishment.

Lytton's Son

Killed in Plane Crash

Reuters, London, 1st - James Lytton, son of Lord Lytton, was killed in an accident yesterday afternoon while piloting a Royal Air Force plane at the Hendon Aerodrome. James Lytton was only thirty years old, a famous boxer, and wrote extensively on various sports. He was a Conservative Member of Parliament and served as a pilot in the London Air Bombing Squadron.

Reuters, London, 1st - The British Auxiliary Air Force is scheduled to perform at the Hendon Aerodrome on May 7. James Lytton, son of Lord Lytton, was practicing with the famous aviator Harrison when the plane crashed upon landing. The plane caught fire. Nearby firefighters rushed to the scene, but before they could help, the plane was destroyed by the fire. The firefighters pulled two people from the fire. James Lytton was already dead, and Harrison was barely alive and died soon after being taken to the hospital. Lord Lytton has two sons and two daughters. The deceased was his eldest son.

Peruvian President Assassinated

Shot by Opposition Party During Military Parade

Assassins and Guards Killed and Wounded

New President Elected, Nationwide Martial Law Declared

Associated Press, Lima, 30th - Peruvian President Cerro was shot and assassinated today at the Tapetitrique racetrack after finishing a military parade. He died shortly after at an Italian hospital. The Peruvian Congress immediately convened an emergency meeting tonight and, within minutes, elected General Benavides, former president and commander of the air force, as the new president. Benavides was inaugurated tonight and declared nationwide martial law. At the same time, the Peruvian cabinet resigned as a matter of course, but the new president announced tonight that he would try to retain them.

Former Peruvian President Cerro, wanting to deal with the undeclared war with Colombia abroad and suppress the rebellions that have been occurring in various parts of the country since last year, had conscripted 20,000 reservists aged between 21 and 23 in February. Today was their first inspection. After the military parade, as he and his cabinet were leaving the field, he was suddenly shot. Multiple opposition party members crowded next to the president's car, and three people jumped onto the running board and opened fire. The first bullet hit the president's vital parts, and he fell into the car. The guards opened fire in retaliation, and there was indiscriminate shooting. The leader of the assassins was killed on the spot. Two soldiers were killed and five were wounded. One of the assassins was seriously wounded, and the rest were arrested. The president was rushed to the Italian hospital after being injured, but died of his injuries.

According to the assassin, the incident was purely political in nature. Since the civil unrest that had been occurring in various places last year and the establishment of the new constitution in February of this year, all political parties had been dissolved, but they continued to operate in practice. Among them was the radical Revolutionary Alliance Party, which called for major political reforms, the overthrow of large landowners, and the implementation of a completely new financial system. The president then ordered the ban on its meetings and the prohibition of the party's slogans. Although the president was intimidated at the time, he was unmoved. The party then claimed that during visits to political prisoners, they discovered that several party members had been secretly executed. Opposition to the government intensified. The assassin, named Dimendo Chai, was a member of the party. The new president, after taking office tonight, ordered the arrest of the party's leaders. Several people have already been arrested.

All government offices across the country are under strict guard, but the capital is as peaceful as usual, and there are no reports of unrest from the provinces. The new president belongs to the Revolutionary Union, the same party as the former president. It is expected that his policies will not change much.

Reuters, Peruvian Capital, 30th - After the assassination of Peruvian President Cerro, there was a clash between soldiers and civilians on the road. Several people were killed and many were injured on both sides.

Reuters, Peruvian Capital, 1st - Martial law has been declared throughout Peru. The new president, General Pinavites, who was appointed by the cabinet last night, was formerly the ambassador to the United Kingdom.

American Shipbuilding Plan

National News, Washington, 1st - Today, U.S. Secretary of the Navy Swanson went to the White House to discuss the naval shipbuilding plan with the president for a long time. Afterwards, Swanson told people that he hoped that the president would include a shipbuilding fund of $460 million in the public works bill to be submitted to Congress within two weeks. Green, president of the American Federation of Labor, had previously suggested a public works construction fund of $300 million, with $30 million allocated to shipbuilding.

British Parliament Discusses

New Anglo-German Trade Agreement

Anglo-Argentine Trade Agreement Signed

Close Cooperation Sought Between Britain and Persia

Reuters, London, 1st - The recent Anglo-German trade agreement was the subject of criticism in the House of Commons today. Minister of Trade Runciman moved to reduce the existing tariffs related to this agreement. Austin Chamberlain, because the Birmingham constituency he represents will be hit by this agreement, especially the jewelry industry, denounced the Anglo-German trade agreement as useless to Britain. He proposed that the House adjourn so that it could consult with all parties concerned. Former Colonial Secretary Amery and Alexander, chairman of the British Manufacturers' Association, both agreed with Chamberlain's remarks. Alexander said that the tariffs produced by the Ottawa Conference and the British Imperial Tariff Advisory Board may be severely damaged by this agreement. Furthermore, the government did not consult with all parties concerned before the agreement was concluded. Runciman claimed that if Chamberlain's motion was passed by the House, the government would not be able to conduct trade agreement negotiations. He has already achieved a good trade agreement. If the House does not want it, then he will have to find someone else to negotiate. Chamberlain's motion was then put to a vote and rejected by 269 votes to 80. Runciman's proposal to reduce the various tariffs related to this agreement was passed by 285 votes to 33.

Reuters, London, 1st - The newly concluded treaty between Britain and Argentina was signed today at the Foreign Office. Foreign Secretary Simon could not attend due to a cold, so Trade Minister Runciman represented Britain in signing the agreement.

Reuters, London, 1st - According to the Daily Express, the compromise between Britain and Persia over the oil dispute has opened the way for a British-Persian treaty. The King of Persia has agreed to send a plenipotentiary to London to negotiate a treaty so that the two countries can closely cooperate in commerce and diplomacy. The treaty will specifically address the elimination of Soviet Russian influence on the Northern Persian Railway and connect Iraq and India by rail.
