Shanghai Morning Talk

— Yiping

Flower Market

Shanghai | A dark hell. Raising your head, you can't see what the sky looks like; if you happen to look out from the window of a small building, you only see a gray-white corner, broken by tall buildings; you can't see flowers, you can't see trees. I know that the dog sign that says "Dogs and Chinese are not allowed" has already been removed, and I've also seen foreign children throwing balls outside the iron fence. But on our own land, there still stands a black-toothed foreigner. The price of a silver dollar can be squandered in five minutes at a dance hall; but in the pockets of the poor, they are reluctant to put that money into the rice shop's till even after a whole month; I finally looked at the place where foreign children throw balls inside and outside the iron fence, and tightly grasped that snow-white silver dollar to return. For the sake of my job, I often step into magnificent guest rooms, where small, exquisite vases on the desk are filled with fresh flowers of all seasons, which makes me wonder if the flowers in Shanghai are mysterious monsters. But since I can't afford the few yuan per month to obtain them, I'm too embarrassed to ask people where my beloved flowers come from. This question was solved in a high-priced night of sleeplessness.

Coming out of the newspaper office, a group of people wandered towards Xiao Wang's house. Stepping out of the iron gate of Nanyang, the fragrance that refreshes the heart and spleen welcomes my nostrils in the breeze, it is the fragrance of flowers. The doors of the Wanhua Building | Small Teahouse | are filled with various kinds of flowers, and when they enter my eyes, I jump up like a child. Inside the Wanhua Building, there are even more expensive flower exhibitions. I did not solicit the opinions of my companions. I stepped into the Wanhua Building from the crowd, and the tea shop boy stopped me, saying: "Sir, I'm sorry, the flower market does not sell tea to guests." I stood there without saying a word, not knowing how to answer him. Xiao Wu and the others had already squeezed up and smiled, saying: "Can we borrow a stool and sit outside the door? We really like flowers." The flower shop boy readily gave us a stool. The flower market extends from Nanyang Bridge to the intersection of Lafayette Road. Middle-aged men with their trouser legs rolled up to their thighs, old women with curved backs, and young women on Nanjing Road shouting "Do you want white orchid?" are all discussing prices for their harvests, preparing to sell them to the people of the city for decorations on their desks after dawn.

Looking at these many flowers that have not yet bloomed, I feel sorry for them. You are sent to Shanghai from the distant countryside, only to be offered on the desk for one day. The second time it dawns, you have already been discarded into the trash can. Your life is so short!

I even imagine the courtyard of my hometown, in which there are dozens of pots of Schlumbergera that I planted myself. Since I drifted to Shanghai, have your destinies suffered the same encounters as mine? Returning to the small building, a paper flower on the desk nods frequently to me. Since I moved into the small building, it has always maintained its due freshness. Because I don't have fresh flowers, I especially protect it, and it still smiles enchantingly at people! Flowers, this is your destiny. You treat people with a pure heart, but inevitably you are grabbed and thrown into the trash can; those painted red and green, on the other hand, can survive in this world!

The Life of the Five Geishas

— Ling He

One. Prologue

Since I am a person who makes a living by writing, most of my time is spent between the tip of the pen and the ink dots. But I cannot help but be scolded as a "literary beggar," almost bordering on shamelessness. Originally, such ridicule is indeed very embarrassing, and several times I was simply so angry that my face turned red and my ears turned red, and I showed my anger on my face, and even wanted to use all my strength to spit at him, and then wrestle with him once, but after calmly thinking about it, I am in fact already like this. I cannot immediately put down my pen and immediately become a gentleman, not to mention that I have never hung up the sign of ARTFORART, so soon, I will be able to take it calmly. Now I write and perhaps I will have to write again later.

But writing articles is not easy. At least in terms of structure, it is difficult to find a subject that I think is satisfactory. I think anyone who can write probably feels the same way. Then now I have to thank my neighbor.

This man's surname is Wu, and his given name is Gui. It is originally a very remarkable name, and just in terms of the word Gui, he himself should be developed a bit, but sometimes when you shout his name and surname quickly, it is inevitable that it is not very elegant to hear. However, he is always called that way by people intentionally or unintentionally, and although some children cannot help but laugh, he does not care. From this, it can be seen that his magnanimity is indeed very great.

Then, my acquaintance with him is of course because he is my neighbor, as mentioned above, and I can often see him, but he also has such an interesting name, so I am unconsciously more aware of him.

It was a hot evening. Because the weather was too hot, the little pug was still panting with its tongue out. At this time, the wife and the teacher's wife were mostly playing cards or listening to the radio broadcast on the balcony; the nanny and the ama were fanning themselves with palm fans next to the car in the alley. At that time, Wu Gui was also sitting on a small stool, sandwiched between the women, chatting and laughing, looking very leisurely.

When I walked up to him in slippers, he quickly and politely got up to give me a seat. He is always so polite, and always calls me "Master" and "Master." Although I always feel that I don't have that kind of status, but since he has to do it this way, I will just let him call me that way, anyway, in this world, it is inevitable that everyone is polite to each other.

— Shi Nong

"Sir, now that Rehe has fallen and North China is in danger, please donate some money to buy planes to resist foreign aggression. Sir, we are both Chinese, and I think you must be very generous," said the person soliciting donations for airplanes to save the country sincerely.

That gentleman was indeed a little moved, and reached into his pocket to take out a ten-yuan bill and waved it at the solicitor. The solicitor smiled and said:

"Oh, sir, you are truly a patriot!"

But the gentleman hesitated and put his hand holding the bill back in. He thought:

"It's too uneconomical to donate ten yuan to someone else. This ten yuan can buy a beautiful dress for my lover..." Those charming eyes and smiling face flashed before his eyes.

He reached into his pocket and exchanged it for a five-yuan bill.

"Take it," he thought. But then he thought again, five yuan can buy a rich meal... Miss Wang's watch hasn't been bought yet? ..."

So, suddenly, his hand reached back into his pocket from the outside.

"Hey! Sir..." the solicitor became impatient.

This time, the gentleman really took out a shiny Yuan head and handed it to the solicitor.

"Okay... the volunteers of modern Northeast thank you, sir!" The solicitor took the money and left.

The gentleman stood on the road in a daze, thinking randomly:

"One yuan can buy the foreign dolls and cookies that the children want... why not give him a few cents?

Alas! It's too wasteful."

Store Clerk Communication

Beast Soldier

Dear Editor,

I am an ignorant and naive person. I am only twenty-one years old this year. I was married by my parents when I was nineteen years old. We both have very good feelings. I only came to Shanghai in early April this year. I was introduced to study medicine at a certain hospital. Recently, I received a letter from home telling me that there was a military disaster there, and my wife was raped by soldiers. According to my parents' wishes, they want her to go out freely, because this is related to the face of our family. The letter is asking for my opinion: But when I think of how good her love for me was in the past, she has never blushed once in the past two years. If I want to keep her, my parents will not allow it; if I don't keep her, my heart really can't bear it. This makes me feel conflicted. I hope you can teach me something, it is my sincere prayer. I wish you

Peace and well-being Zhang Zhiqiang bowed

X X X X

Editor's note: Rape is not a crime, so it can be a condition for divorce for two reasons. (1) Because love cannot accommodate more than one person at the same time, if he or she has already belonged to someone else, of course, his love for his wife or her love for her husband will fade. It is better to divorce frankly than to be together in appearance but separated in spirit. (2) Because human nature inevitably has a possessive desire, especially for the object of love, this possessive thought is particularly strong. Therefore, the facts of adulterers poisoning their husbands and mistresses plotting to harm their wives are endless. For safety, there is only one way to divorce.

Now, Zhang Jun's wife was raped by soldiers; her love for Zhang Jun, of course, has not shaken at all. And if you can forgive her, and comfort her with kind words for this encounter, her love for you will only be stronger, and there will absolutely be no problems.

As for soldiers raping women, it is purely a bestial act of venting lust, and there is no love involved at all. They rape a woman here today, and tomorrow they go to another place to rape another woman. They completely put yesterday's woman out of their minds, and never come back to continue courting her, or even stage a murder of her husband. Therefore, the future of Zhang Jun and his wife will not be in any danger because of this unfortunate event.

Based on the above arguments, we believe that Zhang Jun has no reason to separate from his wife. In terms of human feelings, you should pity her; in terms of law, you cannot treat your wife like this. The responsibility for this matter lies entirely with the illegal soldiers and their officers.

You say that if you keep her, your parents will not allow it; we don't think this is necessarily the case. Since they wrote to solicit your consent, of course, you still have room to speak. As for the matter of face, it is even less of a problem; you must know that if you keep your wife, people will laugh at you, and of course you cannot prevent them from doing so. But you must understand that this is their own lack of knowledge, and it has nothing to do with you.

Lovely Fahua Shan People of Zhejiang Qufu

Movie Special

Movie Reviews

Review of "Moral Treasure Mirror"

— Ling He

Superficially exposes the illusion of "old morality"

In fact, it is preaching for "old morality"

Since the release of "Mad Torrent" and "The Cry of Women," the Star Film Company has in fact embarked on a new path. Of course, this change should be considered a good phenomenon in the Chinese film industry. But there are also questionable points in this. For example, "The Pipa's Spring Complaint" is close to supporting feudal forces, and this "Moral Treasure Mirror" is also preaching for old morality. At the same time, we remember that the Lianhua Film Company's "Night in the City" was criticized by the general public, but now the conclusion of "Moral Treasure Mirror" puts forward the slogan "Go to the countryside," which is undoubtedly not what our audience can accept.

In order to promote Chinese films on the right path with a firm and upright spirit, we must offer some necessary opinions to the authors of this film.

After watching this film, our audience should recognize that the director Wang Xianzhai and the screenwriter Li Nansha have indeed used a spirit of great fearlessness to expose the inside story of pseudo-morality: Zhuang Shoudao used "ancient morality and warm heart" to seduce Xiuzhu, embezzled public funds, and did not hesitate to plot money and kill, and then abandoned his ex-wife to favor a new lover, used fake military power to seize his son, and bought off lawyers to collude in deception, taught his son to follow the rules, but he himself fornicated with the maid; these all allow the audience to understand how hypocrites deceive and harm people.

But what do the authors of this film tell us later? Shoudao's son, Zhuang, died for "morality" out of shame and indignation, and Xiuzhu and her daughter went to the countryside out of hatred for the evils of the city.

Of course, in the semi-feudal Chinese society, because of the inability to abolish the private system, everyone is running around day and night with selfish and self-interested feelings, but this is definitely not a moral issue, but an actual bread issue. Precisely for this reason, how many hypocrites use the good name of morality as a tool for exploitation and deception. On the other hand, of course, there are also those who are deceived and exploited, struggling to survive in pain, and even women cannot help but sell their souls and bodies to associate with young masters. But, can we also explain these with the word "morality"? Of course, this presents a serious economic problem. Therefore, we must point out the importance of moral issues in a society with an economic system, and the inevitable destruction of the "morality" of feudal forces in a capitalist society, so we must not protect morality for the sake of morality, because it has already lost its existence: so there is no need for Zhuang Zhiqing to die for morality, not to mention that a young master who is intoxicated by the real society will not actually commit suicide due to a temporary discovery of conscience. As for the feudal countryside, it will never be "purer" than the city, not to mention that everyone already knows that "this road is impassable." At the same time, it does not seem necessary to use this scene in the progress of the plot, which is inevitably superfluous. In short, I think that in our works, when a problem cannot be solved, it is better not to solve it so that it can cause people to think deeply.

As for the technique, we can somewhat see that Wang Xianzhai, who is directing for the first time, does have experience in photography and is also quite clever, such as Zhuang Zhiqing calling the dancer, and the father stealing and reading his son's pornographic books. However, the entanglement between Qiu Yan and her daughter and Zhiqing has not been systematically explained. Is it saying that she and her daughter colluded to obtain money, or is it saying that she and he already had love and obtained the consent of her mother? There are other shortcomings, but I can't remember them all at once.

Commentary on "Slaying the Whale, A Love Story"

— Jie Ke

Superficial Plot, Excellent Performance

Ordinary Direction, Excellent Cinematography

City audiences, accustomed to films set against the backdrop of urban life (with exceptions, of course, like "Grand Hotel"), find it relatively easy to welcome a change of pace with films set against the backdrop of mountains and fields or the historical dramas of director Cecil B. DeMille. From the standpoint of the film industry, it's also a considerable outlet. Cathay's premiere of "Slaying the Whale, A Love Story" yesterday used whaling ships as its selling point. While it cannot be said to be a top-notch film, it still proved quite engaging. In any case, it's a significant improvement over the last two films, which were almost perfunctory. Although there was no newsreel before the main feature, the musical numbers and cartoons that took its place were a definite improvement over the previous film's tiresome dog act.

The plot of "Slaying the Whale, A Love Story" is simple and superficial, but some of the twists and turns may be difficult for those who haven't read the synopsis beforehand to understand. The film opens with an inscription commemorating the havoc wreaked by the giant whale "Moby Dick" on American coastal shipping, which is acceptable. However, the relationship between the young heroes Ahab and Daniel as brothers is not very clear. The fact that Ahab, after accumulating capital seven years later, acquired his own ship and became its captain is also not very clear. The sailors' mutiny and Ahab's use of force to suppress it are also not clearly depicted.

The film's storyline is based on Herman Melville's novel "Moby Dick." The setting is between 1838 and 1850, so 19th-century costumes are used. The cinematography of the sea ships and whaling scenes in the film is very good. The lighting and framing of the scene where Ahab and the minister's daughter, Phyllis, meet at home is very gentle and charming. The lighting in the wharf and inn scenes is too poor. Perhaps the filmmakers wanted to show the conditions of the 19th century, but the Singapore scene is very well done. This film is somewhat like a dubbed version of an old silent film, but this is not certain.

John Barrymore, who plays the hero Ahab, gives an excellent and energetic performance. Joan Bennett, who plays the minister's daughter Phyllis, is also very gentle and moving. Her enunciation is the clearest and most pleasant to listen to. The entire film consists only of individual actions, with little direction to speak of, resulting in scenes that seem disjointed. The other actors are merely echoing voices.

Joan Crawford and Franchot Tone Finally Announce Their Divorce

— Zhu Xian

The long-rumored divorce case of Joan Crawford and Franchot Tone has now come to an end. The May issues of American film magazines each contain an article documenting this major event in the American film industry. Ironically, they each claimed to have exclusive interviews with Joan Crawford, but all the newspapers ended up having the same information. I will now compile the accounts from various film magazines, extracting the main points as follows:

Joan Crawford and Franchot Tone are not divorcing, but separating, which is the most important point Joan Crawford announced to the film magazine reporters. The difference between divorce and separation is: if they were divorced, both parties would be free to marry again without interference from the other party; but they are only separating, and neither party intends to marry again. They are now living apart but have not completed the legal procedures for divorce, so if either party wishes to remarry in the future, the legal procedures for divorce will need to be completed.

This separation, although only referred to as a separation, has been agreed upon by both parties and has legal effect, meaning that neither party is obliged to fulfill the marital duties of cohabitation. Therefore, it is also called a "legal separation." Whether there is such a provision or term in the law is not investigated here, but it is known that Joan Crawford and Franchot Tone have both agreed to adhere to it firmly. Some say that their separation this time is only temporary, and there may still be hope for reconciliation in the future. However, according to those close to both parties, they have definitively ruled out the possibility of cohabiting again. The reason is that their separation this time was the final decision made out of desperation. It is said that they have actually been separated for eight months, and during those eight months, they tried every possible way to restore their previous level of love, but all failed. They also traveled to Europe, hoping to use the power of a second honeymoon to salvage their fading romance. Unfortunately, that second honeymoon was only like an anesthetic to relieve pain, temporarily relieving the pain but not removing the source of the disease. Therefore, after they returned to Hollywood, they immediately realized that there was no hope of recovering their past love. So, after a long period of consideration, mutual discussion, and with the approval of the experienced old Franchot Tone, they separated. This was an extremely careful decision, leaving no room for reconciliation.

What are the reasons for their separation? According to Joan Crawford's own account, it has nothing to do with jealousy, nor is there a third party involved. She said that she likes boyfriends, but her boyfriends are also friends of her husband; she likes to dance, but when she goes out, her husband often goes with her, or there must be other friends accompanying her, and she has never gone out alone with a boyfriend. As for her husband's girlfriends, she also knows them and often invites them to her house. Therefore, neither she nor her husband had an affair with anyone else. This is why she only mentions separation and not divorce. Joan has no intention of remarrying. She said, "My first marriage has already failed; why try a second time? As for Douglas (Franchot Tone's first name), he also has no intention of remarrying in the near future."

So, why did they separate? More on this tomorrow.

Clara Bow Adopts Twin Children

— Xun

This publication recently reported that Clara Bow, while in France, did not buy foreign clothes but exclusively used American domestic goods, which has aroused considerable praise from this publication's readers, saying that this "hot" lady is enthusiastic about domestic goods, unlike the fashionable women in our country. Now news has come that this Ms. Bow has adopted a pair of twin boys and girls from a poor family, which shows that patriotism begins with love for one's family: doing good must start with one's own brothers. It is quite different from those "charity eaters" in our country who donate thousands or tens of thousands to the poor outside, but turn a cold shoulder to relatives who borrow from them once or twice, which shows that their "goodness" is fake and their wealth is scraped from others. Clara Bow and her husband Rex Bell returned to Europe and their former residence. She gave many gifts to poor relatives, at least ensuring that they would not suffer from cold or hunger for a winter. In the midst of this economic downturn in America, this kind of good deed is a great blessing to them. One day, the couple went to a humble family's house and saw the lovely Lili, and they wanted to take her to Hollywood. But Lili and John are not only twins, but also very loving. John, seeing that Lili was about to leave him, was overcome with grief and cried. Later, Clara, not wanting to see the twins, brother and sister, who were born from the same mother's womb, receive different education and treatment and become people of two different classes in the future, so she took John along as well.

Public Screening of "The Moral Compass"

— Yun

The Mingxing Film Company's new film "The Moral Compass" (formerly known as "The Thief of Humanity") premiered on the second at the Central Theater. The film is a powerful satire of the hypocrisy of false philanthropists. The acting is quite commendable, and the direction is also quite clever.

This publication is a film publication dedicated to supporting cultural and artistic promotion. For external…compensation…too…crude…once a piece of writing is published…the copyright…is owned…by all.

Unless specifically stated in advance and return postage is included, this publication is not responsible for preserving or returning writings, photos, etc.

Submissions that are submitted to multiple publications or are copied writings or recorded statements will not be compensated upon discovery.

Film Novel 42nd Street (Part 4)

— Si Ping

When the dance practice dismissed, Pantell was still outside the theater. Pantell saw Dorothy run off with Abner Dillon, and felt frustrated, but he cheered up a lot when he saw Pankie. Pantell was older than Billy Lawler, but also a bit more handsome in some ways. Pantell made a few passes at Pankie, and they went out for dinner. After dinner, they rode the bus back to Forty-second Street together, and had become bosom friends. Pankie saw that Pantell was a bit depressed, and asked him what was making him sad. Pantell smiled wryly and told her the story of his love affair with another successful chorus girl, and asked for her opinion on the matter. Pankie advised him to start over.

Before closing the door, Pankie looked back frequently, signaling her goodnight to Pantell. On one of her last glances, she spied two shadows closing on his body on the curb. One of them just managed to say something.

"We've got a message for someone called Pantell. Buttnin," he threatened. "If he doesn't lay off Dorothy Brock, he's gonna get a beating! Buttnin, got it?"

Before the other man could answer, the first man reached out with his right hand and punched Pantell hard. Pantell fell to the ground with a thud, and the first thug immediately jumped into the waiting car, while the second thug stayed behind to kick the fallen man hard in the ribs before jumping into the car and speeding away.

Pankie screamed in terror and ran down the steps to help Pantell up.

The next day, Pantell accepted an offer from a theater in Philadelphia, preparing to leave without saying goodbye to Dorothy. But as Pantell packed his bags, Dorothy suddenly arrived.

Pantell felt a heavy weight in his heart and didn't have the courage to kiss her goodbye, because he knew, and she knew, that after a kiss, they wouldn't be able to bear it. Pantell got up and walked to the window. Dorothy didn't wipe away her tears either, and blindly groped towards the door. "Goodbye, Pantell," he choked out.

Pantell didn't turn around. (To be continued)
